end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT</annotation></semantics></math>, Sigma Aldrich) were patterned and sequentially cleaned. After drying with N<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.1">2</sub>, they were treated with UV-Ozone (Ossila Ltda) for 15 minutes to ensure optimal surface cleanliness. A compact Nb<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.2">2</sub>O<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.3">5</sub> layer was deposited via reactive magnetron sputtering in a Kurt J. Lesker System. The deposition was conducted at 500 <sup class="ltx_sup" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.4"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.4.1">o</span></sup>C with 240 W plasma power. The chamber was maintained at a pressure of <math alttext="5.0\times 10^{-3}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1"><semantics id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1a"><mrow id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.cmml"><mn id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.2" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.2.cmml">5.0</mn><mo id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.1" lspace="0.222em" rspace="0.222em" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.1.cmml">×</mo><msup id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.cmml"><mn id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.2" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.2.cmml">10</mn><mrow id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3.cmml"><mo id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3a" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3.cmml">−</mo><mn id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3.2" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3.2.cmml">3</mn></mrow></msup></mrow><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1b"><apply id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1"><times id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.1"></times><cn id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.2.cmml" type="float" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.2">5.0</cn><apply id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3"><csymbol cd="ambiguous" id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3">superscript</csymbol><cn id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.2">10</cn><apply id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3"><minus id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3"></minus><cn id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3.2.cmml" type="integer" xref="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1.1.3.3.2">3</cn></apply></apply></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1c">5.0\times 10^{-3}</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS1.p1.6.m6.1d">5.0 × 10 start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT - 3 end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT</annotation></semantics></math> Torr, with a 40 sccm flow of high-purity argon and 3.5 sccm of oxygen. A mesoporous TiO2 solution (150 mg/ml in ethanol) was spin-coated on top of the Nb<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.5">2</sub>O<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.6">5</sub> compact layer. Both compact and mesoporous layers were annealed at 550 C for 60 minutes. FTO/Nb<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.7">2</sub>O<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.8">5</sub>/TiO<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.9">2</sub> substrates were transferred to a nitrogen-filled glovebox for device fabrication. A Cs<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.10"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.10.1">0.17</span></sub>FA<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.11"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.11.1">0.83</span></sub>Pb(I<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.12"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.12.1">0.83</span></sub>Br<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.13"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.13.1">0.17</span></sub>)<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.14">3</sub> double-cation mixed-halide perovskite solution was prepared by combining two separately prepared solutions: one iodide-based (1.2 M PbI<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.15">2</sub>, 1.0 M FAI, 0.2 M CsI in DMF:DMSO, 4:1 v/v) and one bromide-based (1.2 M PbBr<sub class="ltx_sub" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.16">2</sub>, 1.2 M FABr in DMF:DMSO, 4:1 v/v). The perovskite film was deposited via spin-coating: first at 1000 rpm for 10 s, then at 6000 rpm for 25 s, with 200 <math alttext="\mu" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS1.p1.19.m19.1"><semantics id="S4.SS1.p1.19.m19.1a"><mi id="S4.SS1.p1.19.m19.1.1" xref="S4.SS1.p1.19.m19.1.1.cmml">μ</mi><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS1.p1.19.m19.1b"><ci id="S4.SS1.p1.19.m19.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p1.19.m19.1.1">𝜇</ci></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS1.p1.19.m19.1c">\mu</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS1.p1.19.m19.1d">italic_μ</annotation></semantics></math>L of chlorobenzene (anti-solvent) dropped after 20 s. The perovskite film was first annealed at 60<sup class="ltx_sup" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.17"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.17.1">o</span></sup>C for 3 minutes and then at 120<sup class="ltx_sup" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.18"><span class="ltx_text ltx_font_italic" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.18.1">o</span></sup>C for 30 minutes to promote crystallization. The hole transporting layer (HTL) was based on Spiro-OMeTAD (73 mg/mL in chlorobenzene) doped with 29 <math alttext="\mu" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS1.p1.22.m22.1"><semantics id="S4.SS1.p1.22.m22.1a"><mi id="S4.SS1.p1.22.m22.1.1" xref="S4.SS1.p1.22.m22.1.1.cmml">μ</mi><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS1.p1.22.m22.1b"><ci id="S4.SS1.p1.22.m22.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p1.22.m22.1.1">𝜇</ci></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS1.p1.22.m22.1c">\mu</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS1.p1.22.m22.1d">italic_μ</annotation></semantics></math>L of 4-tert-butyl pyridine, 29 uL of FK209 cobalt complex solution (300 mg/mL in acetonitrile), and 18 <math alttext="\mu" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.m23.1"><semantics id="S4.SS1.p1.23.m23.1a"><mi id="S4.SS1.p1.23.m23.1.1" xref="S4.SS1.p1.23.m23.1.1.cmml">μ</mi><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.m23.1b"><ci id="S4.SS1.p1.23.m23.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS1.p1.23.m23.1.1">𝜇</ci></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.m23.1c">\mu</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.m23.1d">italic_μ</annotation></semantics></math>L of lithium bis(trifluoromethanesulfonic)imide (Li-TFSI) solution (520 mg/mL in acetonitrile). Finally, an 80 nm gold electrode was thermally evaporated onto the device integrated to the Glove Box. More details on the depositions can also be found in the previous publication <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite"><sup class="ltx_sup" id="S4.SS1.p1.23.19.1"><a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2502.10805v1#bib.bib18" title="">18</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2502.10805v1#bib.bib19" title="">19</a></sup></cite>.</p>
</div>
<div class="ltx_para" id="S4.SS1.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS1.p2.1">J-V curves were measured using a Keithley 2400 source measurement unit under simulated sunlight (AM 1.5G,<math alttext="100\,mW\,cm^{-2}" class="ltx_Math" start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT - 2 end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT</annotation></semantics></math>) from a Newport Class AAA solar simulator (model 94023AU), calibrated with a certified silicon solar cell. Additional electrical characterization was performed using the PAIOS system (Fluxim AG). Techniques included staircase sweep J-V, where data points are acquired step-by-step for higher precision, and dark injection transients (DIT), which apply a voltage step and measure the resulting transient current. Sinus-IV measurements applied a sinusoidal voltage, plotting the resulting current versus voltage. Impedance spectroscopy (IS) involved applying a small AC signal (50 mV) superimposed on a DC bias and measuring current across a range of frequencies.</p>
</div>
</section>
<section class="ltx_subsection" id="S4.SS2">
<h3 class="ltx_title ltx_title_subsection">
<span class="ltx_tag ltx_tag_subsection">4.2 </span>Analytical model</h3>
<div class="ltx_para" id="S4.SS2.p1">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS2.p1.2">The analytical model employed in this study builds on our previous work <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite"><sup class="ltx_sup" id="S4.SS2.p1.2.1.1"><a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2502.10805v1#bib.bib20" title="">20</a></sup></cite>. In summary, for an arbitrary bias voltage, <math alttext="V" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1a"><mi id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml">V</mi><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1b"><ci id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1.1">𝑉</ci></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1c">V</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS2.p1.1.m1.1d">italic_V</annotation></semantics></math>, the total current density, <math alttext="j_{T}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1"><semantics id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1a"><msub id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.cmml"><mi id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.2" xref="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml">j</mi><mi id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.3" xref="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.3.cmml">T</mi></msub><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1b"><apply id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1"><csymbol cd="ambiguous" id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1">subscript</csymbol><ci id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.2.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.2">𝑗</ci><ci id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.3.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1.1.3">𝑇</ci></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1c">j_{T}</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS2.p1.2.m2.1d">italic_j start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_T end_POSTSUBSCRIPT</annotation></semantics></math>, is decomposed into three independent components,</p>

<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS2.p1.3">where <math alttext="j_{D}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1"><semantics id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1a"><msub id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.cmml"><mi id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.2" xref="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.2.cmml">j</mi><mi id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.3" xref="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.3.cmml">D</mi></msub><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1b"><apply id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1"><csymbol cd="ambiguous" id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1">subscript</csymbol><ci id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.2.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.2">𝑗</ci><ci id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.3.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1.1.3">𝐷</ci></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1c">j_{D}</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS2.p1.3.m1.1d">italic_j start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_D end_POSTSUBSCRIPT</annotation></semantics></math> represents the diode current density. This term represents the current derived from minority carrier diffusion at the boundaries of the depletion (or intrinsic) region</p>

</div>
<div class="ltx_para" id="S4.SS2.p2">
<p class="ltx_p" id="S4.SS2.p2.3">The second term in Eq. <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2502.10805v1#S4.E1" title="In 4.2 Analytical model ‣ 4 Experimental ‣ A New Approach to Characterize Charge Transport and Hysteresis in Perovskite Solar Cells"><span class="ltx_text ltx_ref_tag">1</span></a> describes the displacement current contribution due to the geometric capacitance, <math alttext="C_{g}" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1"><semantics id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1a"><msub id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.cmml"><mi id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.2" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml">C</mi><mi id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.3" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml">g</mi></msub><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1b"><apply id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1"><csymbol cd="ambiguous" id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1">subscript</csymbol><ci id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.2.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.2">𝐶</ci><ci id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.3.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1.1.3">𝑔</ci></apply></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1c">C_{g}</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS2.p2.1.m1.1d">italic_C start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_g end_POSTSUBSCRIPT</annotation></semantics></math>, of the device with area <math alttext="A" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1"><semantics id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1a"><mi id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.cmml">A</mi><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1b"><ci id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1.1">𝐴</ci></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1c">A</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS2.p2.2.m2.1d">italic_A</annotation></semantics></math>. The third term models memory-related contributions, including ionic channels, fluctuations, and potential leakage pathways (labelled with the sub-index <math alttext="i" class="ltx_Math" display="inline" id="S4.SS2.p2.3.m3.1"><semantics id="S4.SS2.p2.3.m3.1a"><mi id="S4.SS2.p2.3.m3.1.1" xref="S4.SS2.p2.3.m3.1.1.cmml">i</mi><annotation-xml encoding="MathML-Content" id="S4.SS2.p2.3.m3.1b"><ci id="S4.SS2.p2.3.m3.1.1.cmml" xref="S4.SS2.p2.3.m3.1.1">𝑖</ci></annotation-xml><annotation encoding="application/x-tex" id="S4.SS2.p2.3.m3.1c">i</annotation><annotation encoding="application/x-llamapun" id="S4.SS2.p2.3.m3.1d">italic_i</annotation></semantics></math>). It is expressed as,</p>

The combination of these terms consistently reproduces memory effects <cite class="ltx_cite ltx_citemacro_cite"><sup class="ltx_sup" id="S4.SS2.p4.2.1.1"><a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2502.10805v1#bib.bib13" title="">13</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2502.10805v1#bib.bib22" title="">22</a>, <a class="ltx_ref" href="https://arxiv.org/html/2502.10805v1#bib.bib23" title="">23</a></sup></cite>, providing a framework to correlate current-voltage characteristics with IS measurements.</p>
